<div id="review_2045698993" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2045698993" />
    <a title="Andy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2199404-andy"><img alt="Andy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1331458678p2/2199404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2045698993?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy" href="/user/show/2199404-andy">Andy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/6563222-earth-abides">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2045698993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1194134087964647478">I know this is supposed to be a sf classic, but I don't get it. Maybe it's the first populating-the-world story. But I don't know. I think that's Genesis. <br/>The main character bothered me. For example, after the roads go bad, it takes this guy (let alone his whole tribe) twenty years to think of looking for a jeep. If this sort of thing bothers you, then the book will drive you crazy, because it's full of similar head-slappers.<br/>The intro by Connie Willis sort of excuses the flatness of the people a</span>
  <span id="freeText1194134087964647478" style="display:none">I know this is supposed to be a sf classic, but I don't get it. Maybe it's the first populating-the-world story. But I don't know. I think that's Genesis. <br />The main character bothered me. For example, after the roads go bad, it takes this guy (let alone his whole tribe) twenty years to think of looking for a jeep. If this sort of thing bothers you, then the book will drive you crazy, because it's full of similar head-slappers.<br />The intro by Connie Willis sort of excuses the flatness of the people and plot by saying the disaster is the main character, but the big pandemic itself is pretty much absent from the book and the stuff about infectious diseases is generally fuzzy science (even for 1949).</span>
  <a data-text-id="1194134087964647478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mBta19qlXkf7+NOGUP7QWinWmrCMepqAs+w/9ffcwJeiPTMFYfuXL1zTZ+enC9qF/4l9eEL3FOfoknlEOp8yDQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Petl5f42LQhHvUhSOvcCRLemmsxvpAikrUX8yis/Q0sHzQw3RWjkYOCW/DPNAgibYfl9BKEphsP2O7p75nyx0Q==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3890510480348295512">George Rippey Stewart was an American toponymist, a novelist, and a professor of English at the University of California, Berkeley. He is best known for his only science fiction novel <i>Earth Abides</i> (1949), a post-apocalyptic novel, for which he won the first International Fantasy Award in 1951. It was dramatized on radio's Escape and inspired Stephen King's <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/149267.The_Stand' title='The Stand' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Stand</a>
</i>.<br/><br/>His 1941 novel <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/121534.Storm' title='Storm' rel='nofollow noopener'>Storm</a>
</i>, f</span>
  <span id="freeText3890510480348295512" style="display:none">George Rippey Stewart was an American toponymist, a novelist, and a professor of English at the University of California, Berkeley. He is best known for his only science fiction novel <i>Earth Abides</i> (1949), a post-apocalyptic novel, for which he won the first International Fantasy Award in 1951. It was dramatized on radio's Escape and inspired Stephen King's <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/149267.The_Stand" title="The Stand" rel="nofollow noopener">The Stand</a>
</i>.<br /><br />His 1941 novel <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/121534.Storm" title="Storm" rel="nofollow noopener">Storm</a>
</i>, featuring as its protagonist a Pacific storm called <i>Maria,</i> prompted the National Weather Service to use personal names to designate storms and inspired Alan Jay Lerner and Frederick Loewe to write the song "They Call the Wind Maria" for their 1951 musical "Paint Your Wagon." <i>Storm</i> was dramatized as "A Storm Called Maria" on a 1959 episode of ABC's Disneyland. Two other novels, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/542429.Ordeal_by_Hunger" title="Ordeal by Hunger" rel="nofollow noopener">Ordeal by Hunger</a>
</i> (1936) and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1269498.Fire" title="Fire" rel="nofollow noopener">Fire</a>
</i> (1948) also evoked environmental catastrophes.<br /><br />Stewart was a founding member of the American Name Society in 1956-57, and he once served as an expert witness in a murder trial as a specialist in family names. His best-known academic work is <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2376121.Names_on_the_Land_A_Historical_Account_of_Place_Naming_in_the_United_States" title="Names on the Land A Historical Account of Place-Naming in the United States" rel="nofollow noopener">Names on the Land A Historical Account of Place-Naming in the United States</a>
</i> (1945; reprinted, <i>New York Review Books</i>, 2008). He wrote three other books on place-names, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3091714.A_Concise_Dictionary_of_American_Place_Names" title="A Concise Dictionary of American Place-Names" rel="nofollow noopener">A Concise Dictionary of American Place-Names</a>
</i> (1970), <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4006540.Names_on_the_Globe" title="Names on the Globe" rel="nofollow noopener">Names on the Globe</a>
</i> (1975), and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1373426.American_Given_Names" title="American Given Names" rel="nofollow noopener">American Given Names</a>
</i> (1979). His scholarly works on the poetic meter of ballads (published under the name George R. Stewart, Jr.), beginning with his 1922 Ph.D. dissertation at Columbia, remain important in their field.<br /><br />His 1959 book <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/615753.Pickett_s_Charge" title="Pickett's Charge" rel="nofollow noopener">Pickett's Charge</a>
</i> is a detailed history of the final attack at Gettysburg.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3890510480348295512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
